# TrackKcal — Complete Product and Technical Reference (llm.txt)

This document is the single, exhaustive product and technical reference for TrackKcal. It is written for an AI assistant that will reason about, maintain, and extend this codebase. Every number, threshold, formula, gating rule, and copy string in it is drawn from the actual source in this repository, so treat it as ground truth for how the product behaves today.

## What TrackKcal is

TrackKcal is an AI powered nutrition tracking app positioned as an "AI nutritionist in your pocket," not "another food logger." It is UAE first and global second, and understands regional foods natively (the PWA tagline is "The AI calorie tracker that knows shawarma"). It is pre launch, targeting Q2 2026. The stack is React Native with Expo (SDK 54, `newArchEnabled: true`), TypeScript, and Supabase for Auth, Postgres with RLS, and Edge Functions on Deno. OpenAI is reached only through a Supabase Edge Function proxy, so the OpenAI key never touches the client. The app is local first: AsyncStorage is the source of truth and writes return immediately, while Supabase syncs in the background and never blocks the UX on a network call. Bundle and package id is `com.trackkcal.app`; EAS project id `cddbc23a-d73d-4d55-a6cc-af95eb1747e7`.

## How to use this document

Read top to bottom for a full model of the product, or jump to a numbered section for a subsystem. When a section states a value, it is cited from code or repo docs; if you need to change behavior, treat the cited file as the source of truth and update it there. Where a value appears as a constant, config, or feature flag, prefer editing the constant over hardcoding a new one. Matrices (premium vs free, thresholds, gating, prompts, micro targets) are presented as tables so they can be diffed against code. Two architectural rules to keep in mind everywhere: premium is `isPremium`, which requires both a `premium` plan and a signed in account with email (never gate on plan alone), and the launch flag `FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH` in [src/config/featureFlags.ts](src/config/featureFlags.ts) is currently `true`, granting premium to every signed in user until paid tiers and RevenueCat go live.

## High level map of the app surface

The app is a single hub plus modals. [App.tsx](App.tsx) wraps everything in ThemeProvider, PreferencesProvider, and UserProvider, then renders [HomeScreen.tsx](src/screens/HomeScreen.tsx), the hub that owns daily logging, the food log, macro and calorie cards, and the calorie bank surface. From Home the user opens modal screens: the two analytics screens [NutritionAnalysisScreen.tsx](src/screens/NutritionAnalysisScreen.tsx) and [WeightTrackerScreen.tsx](src/screens/WeightTrackerScreen.tsx) (both built around insight cards that pass through `isInsightUnlocked` gates), goal setup [SetGoalsScreen.tsx](src/screens/SetGoalsScreen.tsx), plus [SettingsScreen.tsx](src/screens/SettingsScreen.tsx), [SubscriptionScreen.tsx](src/screens/SubscriptionScreen.tsx), [ChatCoachScreen.tsx](src/screens/ChatCoachScreen.tsx), [ReferralScreen.tsx](src/screens/ReferralScreen.tsx), [GrocerySuggestionsScreen.tsx](src/screens/GrocerySuggestionsScreen.tsx), [AccountScreen.tsx](src/screens/AccountScreen.tsx), [QuickSignupScreen.tsx](src/screens/QuickSignupScreen.tsx), [NotificationSettingsScreen.tsx](src/screens/NotificationSettingsScreen.tsx), [IntegrationsScreen.tsx](src/screens/IntegrationsScreen.tsx), [AboutScreen.tsx](src/screens/AboutScreen.tsx), and the admin tool [AdminPushScreen.tsx](src/screens/AdminPushScreen.tsx). The AI system is the heart of the product: nine LLM prompts (food analysis, vision, coach, weekly insights, grocery, deficit/surplus, and others) all routed through `invokeAI` in [src/services/aiProxyService.ts](src/services/aiProxyService.ts), with JSON prompts using strict `json_schema` and caches keyed by prompt hash via [src/utils/promptVersion.ts](src/utils/promptVersion.ts). The calorie bank in [src/utils/calorieBankEngine.ts](src/utils/calorieBankEngine.ts) banks and spends calories across past completed days only and never settles today. The premium model overlays all of this: gating is `isPremium` (plan plus signed in account), softened during launch by `FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH`.

## 1. Product Overview, Vision, Positioning and Market

---

### What TrackKcal is

TrackKcal is an AI powered nutrition tracking app built in React Native + Expo (SDK 54) with TypeScript, Supabase (Auth, Postgres + RLS, Edge Functions on Deno) for the backend, and OpenAI accessed only through a Supabase Edge Function proxy. It is local first: AsyncStorage is the source of truth and Supabase syncs in the background, so the UI never blocks on the network.

The product reframes calorie tracking around natural language. The user logs food by typing, photographing, or speaking ("two chapati and dal", "shawarma and a laban", a photo of a plate) and the AI parses it into foods with calories and the three macros. There is no database to search and no barcode to scan. A Calorie Bank lets the user flex calories across the week instead of a rigid daily cap. A nutrition analysis screen and a weight tracker surface insights that unlock as the user logs. Premium gates the AI coach and the deeper insight and automation features behind a real signed in account.

### One line pitch and positioning

| Field | Value | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Internal pitch (CLAUDE.md) | "AI nutritionist in your pocket," not "another food logger" | CLAUDE.md, Project orientation |
| Positioning one liner (STRATEGY.md) | "An AI nutritionist that speaks your food." | docs/product/STRATEGY.md |
| Full positioning statement | "For people in the UAE who want to eat better but find Western calorie apps blind to their food, TrackKcal is an AI nutritionist in your pocket that understands what they actually eat and tells them what to do about it. Unlike MyFitnessPal and the other loggers, it does not make you search a database." | docs/product/STRATEGY.md |
| Subscription screen tagline (shipped copy) | "Ad-free. Unlimited entries. Cancel anytime." / "Unlock TrackKcal Premium" | src/screens/SubscriptionScreen.tsx:40-41 |

The stance is explicit: TrackKcal is positioned against database-first loggers. The single defining product moment is "food appearing correctly from plain words." STRATEGY.md calls this "the whole game" and says "Everything else is supporting cast."

### The problem it solves

Per STRATEGY.md: calorie tracking works, but almost nobody sticks with it, and the reason is friction, not motivation. Existing apps make the user the data-entry clerk: search a database, pick the right entry out of twenty wrong ones, guess the portion. For regional food it is worse. Searching "machboos" or "karak" or "biryani from the place downstairs" returns nothing useful, so users quit in the first week and blame themselves. TrackKcal removes the data-entry step with natural language plus regional food understanding.

### Target user / ICP (UAE first)

| Attribute | Definition |
|---|---|
| Primary ICP (proposed, not yet confirmed) | UAE resident, 25 to 40, phone first, has tried MyFitnessPal or Lifesum and quit inside two weeks, eats a mix of regional and Western food, wants to lose or maintain weight "without becoming an accountant about it" |
| Secondary | Global user who wants a logger that is actually fast. The UAE wedge "earns the right to expand; it is not the ceiling." |
| Explicitly NOT for | Bodybuilders weighing food to the gram, clinical/medical nutrition, people who enjoy spreadsheets. "Chasing them blunts the wedge." |

The ICP is a hypothesis, not a confirmed decision. STRATEGY.md lists "Exact ICP" as the first open strategic call and instructs: "Confirm or kill it with five real conversations."

### The wedge (why TrackKcal wins)

The wedge is one sentence in STRATEGY.md: "Regional food understanding, delivered through natural language, with zero database search. That is the whole game."

Two flagship differentiators are designed to compound the wedge:

| Differentiator | What it does | Status |
|---|---|---|
| Calorie Bank | Spend and save calories across the week instead of a rigid daily cap. Floors at 1,500 cal/day for men and 1,200 cal/day for women, with macro auto-scaling, and resets weekly on a chosen day | Premium (docs/app-features.md, Premium #3) |
| Insight engine | "The app tells you what your data means, not just what you ate." Insights unlock progressively as the user logs | Premium (insightUnlockEngine gating) |

### Why now

LLMs made natural-language food understanding good enough to replace database search "in the last two years." That capability did not exist when MyFitnessPal was built, and incumbents are "trapped by their database-first UX and their scale." STRATEGY.md frames the window as "the gap between 'the tech works' and 'the incumbents ship it.' That gap is now."

### Business model and monetization stance

TrackKcal is pre-launch. Payments are not live. During launch, a feature flag grants every signed in user the full premium feature set.

| Item | Value | Source |
|---|---|---|
| Launch flag | `FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH = true` — every signed-in user gets premium, no paywall. To be flipped to `false` when paid tiers + RevenueCat go live | src/config/featureFlags.ts:11 |
| Premium definition (non-negotiable) | Premium is true only when there is a signed-in account with email AND a premium entitlement. During launch the email check still gates, so signed-out users get nothing | src/screens/HomeScreen.tsx:174-184 |
| Annual plan | AED 7.50/mo, billed AED 89.99 annually. Labeled "Best Value", default-selected | src/screens/SubscriptionScreen.tsx:73-74 |
| Monthly plan | AED 24.99/mo, billed monthly | src/screens/SubscriptionScreen.tsx:86-87 |
| Free meal cap (planned, currently disabled) | 3 meals/day on free. Code TODO: "Re-enable daily limit (3 meals/day for free users) before launch." Upsell copy offers a 10-day Premium trial | src/screens/HomeScreen.tsx:1422, 1468 |
| Free edit cap | 3 edits/day on free, unlimited on premium | docs/app-features.md, Premium #2 |
| Intended payments provider | RevenueCat | featureFlags.ts:10, HomeScreen.tsx:177 |

The canonical `isPremium` derivation:

```
const isPremium = React.useMemo(() => {
  if (!accountInfo?.email) return false; // MUST be signed in
  if (FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH) return true;
  if (userPlan === 'premium') return true;
  if (accountInfo?.premiumUntil) return new Date(accountInfo.premiumUntil) > new Date();
  return false;
}, [userPlan, accountInfo]);
```

The monetization stance in STRATEGY.md is that the premium model is "honest (gated on a real account plus plan), which builds trust the ad-funded incumbents cannot." The exact free-vs-paid line is an open call: "Where does the AI nutritionist stop being free? This is the whole business model and it is currently a launch flag, not a decision." A referral loop substitutes for early paid access: each referral grants 3 free premium days (docs/app-features.md, Free #11).

### Competitors and differentiation

STRATEGY.md names MyFitnessPal and Lifesum directly; the founder's reference set also includes Yazio and Cal AI.

| Competitor | What they are | How TrackKcal differs |
|---|---|---|
| MyFitnessPal | The incumbent database logger | TrackKcal removes database search entirely; named as "the thing we are replacing." STRATEGY.md: incumbents are "trapped by their database-first UX and their scale" |
| Lifesum | Database/food-search logger | Same wedge: natural language over search. ICP is specifically users who "tried MyFitnessPal or Lifesum and quit inside two weeks" |
| Yazio | Database logger / meal plans | No manual database search as a primary path; no gram-level scale workflows |
| Cal AI | AI photo calorie app | TrackKcal goes beyond photo logging to text + voice + photo, plus Calorie Bank and an insight engine; the regional-food wedge is the differentiator |

The discipline that protects the differentiation (STRATEGY.md, "What we will deliberately NOT do"):

- No manual database search as a primary path. "The moment we add it, we become the thing we are replacing."
- No gram-level scale workflows. "That is a different product."
- No social feed. "Not the wedge, huge maintenance cost."
- No Android Western-market push before the UAE wedge is proven retained.
- No new feature until activation and week-1 retention are measured and healthy.

Stated moat: regional food taste and prompt quality that compounds with every real log (the food-analysis cache tags entries by prompt version, so corrections accumulate); a solo founder who ships fast against slower incumbents; and an honest premium model. STRATEGY.md is candid: "The moat is thin today. It deepens only with retained users and accumulated regional accuracy."

### North Star and key metrics

The product is framed as a habit business: "Not a download business, not a feature business" (METRICS.md).

North Star Metric (proposed): **Weekly Active Loggers** = count of users who logged food on 3 or more distinct days in the last 7. Rationale: opening the app is not value, and one user spamming logs should not inflate the number; 3 days/week is "the threshold where the data becomes useful to the user and the habit starts to hold."

Metric tree (METRICS.md):

| Layer | Definition |
|---|---|
| North Star | Weekly Active Loggers (3+ logging days in last 7) |
| Activation | Aha moment = first successful AI log in the first session. Activation event (proposed) = logged on 3 distinct days within the first 7 |
| Retention | D1, D7, D30; the curve that matters most is Week 1 → Week 2 |
| Logging quality | Log success rate, edit rate, time from tap to logged |
| Revenue (post-payments) | Free→paid conversion; AI cost per active user vs revenue per user |
| Referral | Codes shared, codes redeemed, ratio (K-factor) |

Proposed targets (benchmark-based, METRICS.md):

| Metric | Floor | Good | Strong |
|---|---|---|---|
| D1 retention | 30% | 40% | 50% |
| D7 retention | 15% | 22% | 28% |
| D30 retention | 8% | 12% | 18% |
| Activation (3 logs in 7 days) | 25% | 35% | 45% |
| Log success rate | 85% | 92% | 96% |
| Free to paid (post-payments) | 2% | 4% | 6% |

Instrumentation reality (METRICS.md): events fire into Mixpanel via `analyticsService` (app open/close, meal logged with date, exercise logged, weight logged, onboarding started / goal set / first meal logged, screen opens, voice/camera/photo usage, subscription screen open, saved prompts, smart reminders, referral lifecycle, `identifyUser`). Known gaps: no `food_log_result` (success/clarification/error/no-food) event to measure the wedge directly; no revenue/purchase events yet; AI cost per user must be pulled from the proxy/OpenAI usage, not the client. The flagged risk is anonymous→identified continuity (users log before creating an account; the pre-account device id must be aliased on signup or the first-session funnel breaks). The stated first deliverable is one Mixpanel board: a Week-1 retention cohort plus an activation funnel (install → goal set → first successful log → 3 logs in 7).

The 12-month bet (STRATEGY.md): by Q2 2027, a measured week-1 retention above the category benchmark, a paying conversion that covers AI cost per user, and a UAE word-of-mouth loop. "Not vanity downloads. Retention and unit economics." The founder's nominated single metric not to let slip is week-1 retention.

## 2. Technical Architecture and Stack

### Stack overview

| Layer | Technology | Version / source |
| --- | --- | --- |
| App runtime | React Native | `0.81.5` (`package.json`), New Architecture on (`app.json` `newArchEnabled: true`) |
| Framework | Expo | SDK 54 (`expo ~54.0.25`), `babel-preset-expo ~54.0.10` |
| Language | TypeScript | `~5.9.2`, typecheck via `npx tsc --noEmit` |
| React | React / React DOM | `19.1.0` |
| Navigation | `@react-navigation/native` `^7.1.19`, `@react-navigation/stack` `^7.6.2` | wrapped in `NavigationContainer` (`App.tsx`) |
| Web/PWA | `react-native-web ^0.21.0`, Metro web bundler | `app.json` `web.output: "single"`, `web.bundler: "metro"` |
| Backend | Supabase (`@supabase/supabase-js ^2.86.0`) | Auth, Postgres + RLS, Edge Functions (Deno) |
| AI | OpenAI, reached only through the `ai-proxy` Supabase Edge Function | never called from client |
| Local store | `@react-native-async-storage/async-storage 2.2.0` | source of truth |
| Errors / replay | `@sentry/react-native ^8.12.0` | init in `App.tsx` |
| Animation | `react-native-reanimated ^4.1.3`, `react-native-worklets 0.5.1` | |
| Health | `react-native-health ^1.19.0` (Apple Health), `react-native-health-connect ^3.5.0` (Android) | |
| Media / input | `expo-image-picker`, `expo-av`, `expo-speech`, `expo-clipboard`, `expo-print`, `expo-sharing` | voice + photo logging, export |
| Auth providers | `expo-apple-authentication ~8.0.7`, `expo-auth-session ~7.0.9` (Google) | |
| OTA | `expo-updates ~29.0.17` | `app.json` `updates.url: https://u.expo.dev/cddbc23a-...` |

Bundle ID / package: `com.trackkcal.app` (both iOS `bundleIdentifier` and Android `package`). EAS project id: `cddbc23a-d73d-4d55-a6cc-af95eb1747e7`. Android `minSdkVersion 26` (via `expo-build-properties`). Android runtime permissions declared: `CAMERA`, `READ_MEDIA_IMAGES`, `READ_EXTERNAL_STORAGE`, `RECORD_AUDIO`, `ACTIVITY_RECOGNITION`.

### Provider tree and app entry

Entry is `index.ts` → `App.tsx`. The app is wrapped by `Sentry.wrap(...)`. Sentry is initialized at module load with `replaysSessionSampleRate: 0.1`, `replaysOnErrorSampleRate: 1`, `sendDefaultPii: true`, `enableLogs: true`, and mobile replay + feedback integrations.

Provider nesting (outer to inner), all in `App.tsx`:

```
SafeAreaProvider
  └─ ThemeProvider            (src/constants/theme.tsx)
      └─ PreferencesProvider  (src/contexts/PreferencesContext.tsx)
          └─ UserProvider     (src/contexts/UserContext.tsx)
              └─ NavigationContainer
                  ├─ HomeScreen
                  └─ PasswordRecoveryModal
                  └─ StatusBar (style="dark", bg white)
```

`App.tsx` also runs `useSyncQueueOnForeground()`: on native it calls `dataStorage.flushSyncQueue()` on `AppState` `active`; on web/PWA it flushes on `document` `visibilitychange` → `visible` and once on mount. This drains writes that were queued while offline or signed out.

### Navigation model: HomeScreen hub + modals

There is one real screen. `HomeScreen` is the hub; every other "screen" is a React Native `Modal` rendered from `HomeScreen` and toggled by local boolean state (e.g. `showGrocerySuggestions`). `HomeScreen.tsx` contains 85 modal/visibility references. `NavigationContainer` is present (React Navigation is installed) but routing is effectively flat — there is no stack of pushed routes. The files under `src/screens/` (NutritionAnalysis, WeightTracker, SetGoals, Settings, Subscription, ChatCoach, Referral, GrocerySuggestions, Account, QuickSignup, NotificationSettings, Integrations, About, AdminPush) are modal bodies opened from the hub, not navigator routes. A consequence noted in `CLAUDE.md`: the Settings back handler must reload all derived state in `HomeScreen` because nothing re-fetches on a route transition.

### Contexts and state

State is React Context, not Redux. There are exactly two app-level data contexts plus theme.

| Context | File | Holds | Notable behavior |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `UserProvider` / `useUser` | `contexts/UserContext.tsx` | `goals`, `meals` (keyed `YYYY-MM-DD`), `weightEntries`, `adjustmentAvailable`, `currentStreak`, `streakFreeze`, `accountInfo`, `isLoading`, `lastRefresh` | parallel load via `Promise.all` of 6 `dataStorage` reads; concurrent loads collapsed via `loadInFlightRef`; optimistic `saveMeal`; realtime reload debounce 400ms |
| `PreferencesProvider` / `usePreferences` | `contexts/PreferencesContext.tsx` | `weightUnit` (`'kg' | 'lbs'`, default `'kg'`), conversions | persisted to AsyncStorage key `@trackkal:weightUnit`; kg→lbs `×2.20462`, lbs→kg `×0.453592` |
| `ThemeProvider` / `useTheme` | `constants/theme.tsx` | resolved `Theme` object | see theming below |

`UserContext` drives auth-reactive data flow. Its `authService.onAuthStateChange` listener treats `SIGNED_IN`, `TOKEN_REFRESHED`, and `INITIAL_SESSION` as recoverable signed-in events. On a missing local `AccountInfo` (common cause: iOS Safari ITP cache eviction on PWA) it rebuilds `accountInfo` from the Supabase session and re-saves it. On `SIGNED_IN` it backfills local → Supabase once (`pushDerivedToSupabase`) then pulls (`pullDerivedFromSupabase`); on `INITIAL_SESSION`/`TOKEN_REFRESHED` it only pulls (no push on every launch); then `loadAllData()`. Streak-freeze allowance auto-resets monthly to `freezesAvailable: 2` keyed on `format(new Date(), 'yyyy-MM-01')`.

### Local-first storage and the sync queue

AsyncStorage is the source of truth; Supabase is eventual. `dataStorage.ts` is the single read/write/sync layer. Local writes return immediately and never block on the network.

Sync queue mechanics (`dataStorage.ts`):
- Queue persisted under AsyncStorage key `@trackkal:syncQueue` as a JSON array of `SyncOperation`.
- All read-modify-write on the queue runs inside a named write lock (`withWriteLock('syncQueue', ...)`) so an enqueue and a flush cannot interleave and drop/duplicate ops.
- `SyncOperation` entities: `meal`, `weight`, `goals`, `exercise`, `push_token`, `push_history`, `saved_prompt`, `preferences`, `settings`, `entry_tasks`, `referral_code`, `referral_redemption`, `referral_reward`, `streak_freeze`, `analytics_event`. Actions are `upsert` / `delete` / `log`.
- `processSyncQueue` skips entirely if there is no `accountInfo` with `supabaseUserId` or `email`. It executes each op; on failure it does NOT abort the whole queue (no head-of-line blocking) — it increments a per-op `_attempts` and retries up to `MAX_SYNC_ATTEMPTS = 5`, then drops that op and continues so later ops still sync.
- `processSyncQueue` is invoked after most local saves and on foreground via `flushSyncQueue`.
- Public sync surface on `dataStorage`: `flushSyncQueue()`, `pushDerivedToSupabase()`, `pullDerivedFromSupabase()`.

Meal diffing for sync uses `diffMeals(previous, next)`: flattens both meal maps by `id`, marks new ids as upserts, JSON-compares existing meals to detect changes (touching `updatedAt`), and detects removals as deletions. `ensureMealMetadata` backfills `id` (via `ensureUUID`) and `updatedAt` before sync.

### Soft-delete model

Deletes are soft, server-side, never hard (so a delete on one device cannot be resurrected by an upsert from another). In `supabaseDataService.ts`:
- `deleteMeals` runs `.update({ deleted_at: <ISO now> })` on `food_logs` filtered by `user_id` + `id IN (...)`. Same pattern for exercises and weight entries.
- `fetchMeals` filters live rows with `.is('deleted_at', null)`.
- Full-list upserts deliberately omit `deleted_at` (never send `deleted_at: null`) so re-pushing the whole list does not un-delete a row soft-deleted elsewhere.
- Push tokens are revoked with `revoked_at`; referral/other rows use `is_active: false`.
- The exception is hard account deletion: `supabaseDataService` hard-deletes the user's data tables and the `app_users` row, and the Edge Function (`type: "delete_user"`) admin-deletes the `auth.users` record (App Store compliance).

Note: `food_logs.user_id` stores the `app_users` row id, not the Supabase auth uid. Code that scopes per-user (realtime filter, RLS-bound queries) resolves the `app_users` id via `getOrCreateUser`/`fetchAccountByEmail`.

### Realtime

`realtimeMealsService.ts` opens one Postgres-changes channel per user: `food_logs:user:<appUserId>`, `event: '*'`, `schema: public`, `table: food_logs`, `filter: user_id=eq.<appUserId>`. On any change it calls `invalidateMealsCache()` then the caller's `onChange`. `UserContext` debounces that 400ms, then `loadMeals()` → `setMeals`. Self-fired writes also arrive and are harmlessly reconciled. Requires `food_logs` to be in the `supabase_realtime` publication (`ALTER PUBLICATION supabase_realtime ADD TABLE public.food_logs;`). Only one active channel at a time; switching users tears down the old channel first.

### Supabase client and auth config

`supabaseClient.ts` creates the client only if both `EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL` and `EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` are set; otherwise `supabase` is `null`, `isSupabaseConfigured()` returns false, and remote sync + auth are disabled (the app still works fully local). Auth options: `persistSession: true`, `autoRefreshToken: true`, `storage: AsyncStorage`, and `detectSessionInUrl: Platform.OS === 'web'` (web must consume the recovery/auth token Supabase puts in the URL after a password-reset redirect; native has no URL to parse).

### OpenAI proxy pattern

The OpenAI key is a Supabase Edge Function secret (`OPENAI_API_KEY`) and never reaches the client (`config/env.ts` documents this; `aiProxyService.ts` enforces it). Path: client → `invokeAI` / `invokeWhisper` (`aiProxyService.ts`) → `supabase.functions.invoke('ai-proxy', ...)` → Edge Function (`supabase/functions/ai-proxy/index.ts`, Deno) → OpenAI.

`invokeAI` request shape: `{ model, messages, temperature?, max_tokens?, response_format?, call_type?, timeout_ms?, signal? }`. `response_format` is one of `json_object`, `text`, or `json_schema` (with `name`, optional `strict`, `schema`).

| Knob | Value | Source |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Default timeout | `DEFAULT_AI_TIMEOUT_MS = 60_000` (60s) | `aiProxyService.ts` |
| Edge default chat model | `gpt-4o-mini` (if `body.model` absent) | `ai-proxy/index.ts` |
| Whisper model | `whisper-1`, `language: 'en'`, blob `audio/m4a` | `aiProxyService.ts` / Edge |
| CORS | `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *` | Edge |

Cancellation chains end to end: each call creates an `AbortController`; the timeout (or a caller `signal`) aborts it; supabase-js closes the underlying fetch; that closes `req` inside the Edge Function; the Edge passes `signal: req.signal` to the upstream OpenAI fetch, which stops billing once the socket dies. Errors are unwrapped from `error.context.text()` so logs show the real OpenAI cause (rate limit, schema validation, bad key) rather than a generic non-2xx, and every failure is reported to Sentry with `ai_call_type` / `ai_model` / `ai_timeout` / `ai_aborted` tags. The Edge Function multiplexes on `body.type`: `delete_user` (service-role admin delete, JWT-verified), `transcription` (Whisper), default = chat completions.

### Premium gating model

`isPremium` is derived, not stored as a single flag, and is the only correct gate (`HomeScreen.tsx`):

```ts
const isPremium = React.useMemo(() => {
  if (!accountInfo?.email) return false;        // MUST be signed in
  if (FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH) return true;          // launch flag
  if (userPlan === 'premium') return true;
  if (accountInfo?.premiumUntil) return new Date(accountInfo.premiumUntil) > new Date();
  return false;
}, [userPlan, accountInfo]);
```

| Condition | Result |
| --- | --- |
| Not signed in (no `accountInfo.email`) | never premium, even on a `premium` plan |
| `FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH === true` (current) + signed in | premium |
| `userPlan === 'premium'` + signed in | premium |
| `accountInfo.premiumUntil` in the future + signed in | premium |

`FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH` lives in `config/featureFlags.ts` and is currently `true`: every signed-in user gets premium with no paywall during launch. Flip to `false` when paid tiers + RevenueCat go live. Because the gate still requires a signed-in email, signed-out users are unaffected. `featureFlags.grocerySuggestions.isEnabled` is a separate admin-only gate keyed on `ADMIN_EMAILS` (`admin@trackkcal.com`, `hulexo@trackkcal.com`, `test@trackkcal.com`) and `ADMIN_IDS`. There is a known past bug: gating on plan alone let signed-out free users see premium features; always check both.

### Theming

`theme.tsx` defines a full token set (colors, `radii` sm/md/lg/xl/pill = 4/8/12/16/9999, three `elevation` presets) with both `lightTheme` and `darkTheme`. Dark mode is implemented but disabled for launch: `ThemeProvider` hardcodes `currentMode='light'`, `valueTheme=lightTheme`, and `setMode` always resolves to light. Note the in-app theme background (`#F5F5F5` light) differs from the PWA chrome color (`themeColor`/`backgroundColor` `#FBF9F4` in `app.json` `web`).

### Env and config

| Variable | Where | Purpose |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL` | `supabaseClient.ts` | Supabase project URL |
| `EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` | `supabaseClient.ts` | anon key (public, RLS-protected) |
| `EXPO_PUBLIC_GOOGLE_EXPO_CLIENT_ID` / `_IOS_` / `_ANDROID_` / `_WEB_CLIENT_ID` | `config/env.ts` (`config.GOOGLE_OAUTH`) | Google OAuth client ids |
| `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` (auth, notifications) | `authService.ts`, `notificationService.ts` | additional public config |
| `OPENAI_API_KEY` | Edge Function secret only | OpenAI auth, never on client |
| `SUPABASE_URL`, `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` | Edge Function secrets | service-role admin delete |

Only `EXPO_PUBLIC_`-prefixed vars are exposed to the client bundle (Expo convention). Anything secret (OpenAI key, service-role key) lives exclusively as a Supabase secret.

### App versioning: two separate numbers

These are deliberately decoupled (`appVersion.ts` comment):

| Number | Source | Current | Role |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Display version | `src/constants/appVersion.ts` `APP_VERSION` | `1.3.6` | bumped every commit; shown in Settings so you can tell which build is on a device/PWA |
| Runtime version | `app.json` `version` `1.0.0` + `runtimeVersion.policy: "appVersion"` | `1.0.0` | drives EAS Update `runtimeVersion`; must stay stable or OTA updates stop reaching installed builds |
| Android `versionCode` | `app.json` `android.versionCode` | `1` | Play Store build number, incremented per store release |

Do not bump `app.json` `version` to mark a release — that breaks OTA delivery. Use `APP_VERSION` for human-visible version, `versionCode` for store builds.

### Build and deploy model

Two distribution targets from one codebase.

EAS build profiles (`eas.json`):

| Profile | Distribution | Android output | Channel | Notes |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `development` | internal | `:app:assembleDebug` | `development` | dev client |
| `preview` | internal | `apk` | `preview` | `NODE_OPTIONS=--max-old-space-size=4096`, `SENTRY_DISABLE_AUTO_UPLOAD=true` |
| `production` | store | `app-bundle` (`.aab`) | `production` | for Play submit |

The everyday tester build is the EAS `preview` channel APK (`npx eas build --platform android --profile preview`); it bumps Node heap to 4GB and disables Sentry source-map upload to avoid build OOM. Production store builds use the `app-bundle` profile and `npx eas submit --platform android --profile production` (`docs/RELEASE.md`). OTA updates flow through `expo-updates` against `https://u.expo.dev/cddbc23a-...` matched on `runtimeVersion`.

The web/PWA target is a Metro single-file web export (`app.json` `web.output: "single"`) deployed to Vercel. PWA manifest fields come from `app.json` `web`: `name`/`shortName` `TrackKcal`, `display: "standalone"`, `themeColor`/`backgroundColor` `#FBF9F4`, description "The AI calorie tracker that knows shawarma." The PWA is treated as a temporary tester bridge (per project memory: fix shared bugs, deprioritize PWA-only bugs), and it is the surface most exposed to iOS Safari ITP cache eviction — hence the `AccountInfo` rehydrate-from-session logic in `UserContext` and the visibility-change sync flush in `App.tsx`.

---

What I cut and what to watch:
- I did not enumerate the full Postgres schema, RLS policies, or per-prompt JSON schemas — those belong to the data-model and AI-prompts sections. I documented only the architectural touchpoints (soft-delete columns, app_users-vs-auth-uid, proxy contract).
- I could not find a `memory/trackkcal-deploy-runbook.md` in the repo (the memory index references it but the file is not present under the repo tree). The Vercel/PWA deploy specifics above come from `app.json`, `eas.json`, `docs/RELEASE.md`, and `App.tsx`, not from that runbook. If you want the exact `expo export` + Vercel commands and the RAM/Hermes gotcha quoted verbatim, that runbook needs to be located or recreated.
- Blast radius if any of these facts is wrong in llm.txt: an LLM could (a) bump `app.json` version and silently kill OTA, (b) gate premium on plan alone and leak features to signed-out users, or (c) hard-delete instead of soft-delete and break cross-device sync. All three are real past or guarded-against failure modes in this repo.

Relevant files (all absolute): `c:\Users\Hulexo\Downloads\journafied\journafied-app\App.tsx`, `src\contexts\UserContext.tsx`, `src\contexts\PreferencesContext.tsx`, `src\constants\theme.tsx`, `src\constants\appVersion.ts`, `src\services\aiProxyService.ts`, `src\services\supabaseClient.ts`, `src\services\dataStorage.ts`, `src\services\supabaseDataService.ts`, `src\services\realtimeMealsService.ts`, `src\config\env.ts`, `src\config\featureFlags.ts`, `src\screens\HomeScreen.tsx`, `supabase\functions\ai-proxy\index.ts`, `app.json`, `eas.json`, `package.json`, `docs\RELEASE.md`.

## 3. Onboarding, Goal Setting and the Calorie Calculator

---

The onboarding and goal-setting flow is one of the few experiences in TrackKcal that is fully free and never premium-gated. Setting goals is mandatory for the app to be useful (without goals, the home screen shows only a prompt), so it sits before any paywall. Below is the complete, code-cited reference.

### Where it lives

| Concern | File |
| --- | --- |
| Goal review + macro editor screen | `src/screens/SetGoalsScreen.tsx` |
| Multi-step calculator wizard + result | `src/components/CalorieCalculatorModal.tsx` (exports `CalorieCalculatorScreen`) |
| First-launch carousel | `src/components/AppWalkthroughModal.tsx` |
| Persisted goal model | `ExtendedGoalData` in `src/services/dataStorage.ts` (lines 143-164) |
| Save/load to AsyncStorage + Supabase | `dataStorage.saveGoals` / `dataStorage.loadGoals` |
| Host + state owner | `src/screens/HomeScreen.tsx` |
| Weight-driven re-adjustment (separate feature) | `src/components/SmartAdjustmentModal.tsx` |

Premium status: **none of this is gated.** There is no `isPremium` check anywhere in `SetGoalsScreen.tsx` or `CalorieCalculatorModal.tsx`. The calculator, the macro editor, and the walkthrough are available to every user, signed in or not, free or premium. The only account-related step in the flow is an optional `QuickSignupScreen` shown once after the first-time calculation (see "First-time flow").

---

### The AppWalkthroughModal (first-launch carousel)

Shown once on first launch. `HomeScreen` checks `AsyncStorage.getItem('@trackkal:hasSeenWalkthrough')`; if absent it opens the modal after a `setTimeout` of `1000` ms (`HomeScreen.tsx` line 1139). Closing or skipping writes `'true'` to that key so it never shows again automatically. It can be re-opened from Settings ("How it works"), which sets `walkthroughHideOffer = false` and re-shows it.

Five slides, defined in the `STEPS` array (`AppWalkthroughModal.tsx` lines 37-84):

| # | Title | Tagline | Icon | Accent | Final? |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | "Say it. Snap it. Done." | No typing required | `mic` | `#3B82F6` | no |
| 2 | "Built around your body" | Adapts as you progress | `target` | `#10B981` | no |
| 3 | "See what's really happening" | Trends over time | `trending-up` | `#F59E0B` | no |
| 4 | "Your AI Nutritionist" | Answers based on your data | `message-circle` | `#8B5CF6` | no |
| 5 | "Let's build your plan" | Takes about 2 minutes | `play-circle` | `#06B6D4` | yes |

- The final slide (`isFinal: true`) shows two CTAs: a primary "Get Started" button (calls `onSignUp`) and a secondary "Explore on my own" text link (calls `onClose(true)`).
- A `hideOffer` prop filters out the final slide entirely (`filteredSteps = STEPS.filter(s => !s.isFinal)`). When `hideOffer` is true, the last non-final slide ("Your AI Nutritionist") shows a "Done" button instead of "Next". `HomeScreen` passes `hideOffer={walkthroughHideOffer || isPremium}` so premium/already-signed-in users do not see the signup offer.
- Layout: card is `width - 48` wide, `height * 0.55` tall, `borderRadius: 24`. Horizontal `FlatList`, paging enabled, snaps per `ITEM_WIDTH` (`CARD_WIDTH - 48`). Progress bar animates to `(currentIndex + 1) / filteredSteps.length` over `250` ms. On web/PWA it uses `scrollToOffset` (not `scrollToIndex`) because the latter silently no-ops there.

The walkthrough is purely informational. It collects no data. The "Get Started" path leads into signup/calculator; "Explore on my own" drops the user on the home screen where the set-goals prompt awaits.

---

### The calculator wizard (`CalorieCalculatorScreen`)

A linear, animated, one-question-per-screen wizard. Step order is built dynamically by `buildSteps(goal, hasName)` (`CalorieCalculatorModal.tsx` lines 71-76):

```
hasName ? ['goal','sex','dob','height','weight'] : ['name','goal','sex','dob','height','weight']
+ (goal !== 'maintain' ? ['pace'] : [])
+ ['activity']
```

So the maximum is 8 steps (new user, lose/gain goal) and the minimum is 6 (returning user with a name, maintain goal: goal, sex, dob, height, weight, activity). The `name` step is **skipped whenever a name already exists** (`hasExistingName = !!(initialData?.name && initialData.name.trim().length > 0)`). This is the fix for the past bug where re-evaluating asked for the name twice.

#### Step inputs

| Step | `StepId` | Accent | Input mechanism | Stored as | Validation / notes |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Name | `name` | `#3B82F6` | `TextInput`, `autoFocus`, `maxLength={30}`, `autoCapitalize="words"` | `userName` | Disabled until non-empty (trimmed). Skipped if name exists. |
| Goal | `goal` | `#3B82F6` | 3 cards: Lose / Maintain / Gain | `goal: 'lose'\|'maintain'\|'gain'` | Auto-advances on tap (`autoAdv`, 280 ms delay). Picking `maintain` sets `selectedRate = 0` and removes the pace step. |
| Sex | `sex` | `#8B5CF6` | 3 options: Male / Female / Prefer not to say | `gender` | Auto-advances. "Prefer not to say" is treated as `male` in BMR math (`g = gender === 'prefer_not_to_say' ? 'male' : gender`). |
| DOB | `dob` | `#10B981` | 3 scroll pickers (month / day / year) | `dob` string `YYYY-MM-DD`, plus derived `age` | Age is computed, never typed (`ageFromDob`). |
| Height | `height` | `#10B981` | cm picker, or ft + in pickers; cm/ft toggle | `heightCm` (always), plus `heightFeet`/`heightInches` when ft | Always has a value, never disabled. |
| Weight | `weight` | `#F59E0B` | Two numeric `TextInput`s: current + target (target optional); kg/lbs toggle | `currentWeightKg`, `targetWeightKg` (both stored in kg) | Current required. Target validated on Next. |
| Pace | `pace` | `#EC4899` | 3 cards: 0.25 / 0.5 / 1.0 kg/week | `activityRate` (= `selectedRate`) | Only present when goal ≠ maintain. Auto-advances. |
| Activity | `activity` | `#06B6D4` | 4 cards: Sedentary / Light / Moderate / Very | `activityLevel` | Auto-advances and triggers the result screen directly (`showResultScreen`). |

#### Picker ranges (exact)

- **Months**: 12 entries, displayed as 3-letter abbreviations (`Jan`…`Dec`).
- **Days**: 1-31.
- **Years**: 80 entries starting at `currentYear - 14` and counting down (`YEAR_ITEMS`, lines 173-177). So the youngest selectable DOB is 14 years ago; oldest is `currentYear - 14 - 79`.
- **Height cm**: 120-240 (`121` entries, `120 + i`).
- **Height feet**: 3-7 (`FT_ITEMS`, `3 + i`, 5 entries).
- **Height inches**: 0-11.
- Defaults when no `initialData`: cm = 170, ft = 5, in = 8, dobYear = 2000 (month/day default 1/1), gender/goal/activityLevel = null.

Picker UI: `ScrollPicker` is a snapping `FlatList`, item height `48`, 5 visible items, the centered row highlighted with the step accent at `40` (border) and `08` (fill) alpha.

#### Goal cards copy

| Goal | Label | Description | Icon |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| lose | Lose Weight | Burn fat & get lean | `trending-down` |
| maintain | Maintain Weight | Stay at your current weight | `minus` |
| gain | Gain Weight | Build muscle & mass | `trending-up` |

#### Activity cards copy + multipliers

| `activityLevel` | Label | Description | TDEE multiplier | Breakdown label |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `sedentary` | Sedentary | Office job, little exercise | **1.2** | Sedentary |
| `light` | Lightly Active | 1-3 days/week exercise | **1.375** | Lightly active |
| `moderate` | Moderately Active | 3-5 days/week exercise | **1.55** | Moderately active |
| `very` | Very Active | 6-7 days/week hard exercise | **1.725** | Very active |

Fallback multiplier when no activity is selected is `1.4` labeled "Moderate" (used only in the `calcCaloriesDetailed` fallback path; in practice activity is always chosen before the result screen).

#### Pace options

Generated by `getRateOptions()` (lines 324-332). Labels swap "loss"/"gain" and "lose"/"gain" by goal. The `sub` line appends the projected target date when a target weight is set.

| Rate (`selectedRate`) | Label (lose) | Sub |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 0.25 | Mild weight loss | lose 0.25 kg/week [· date] |
| 0.5 | Weight loss | lose 0.5 kg/week [· date] |
| 1.0 | Fast weight loss | lose 1.0 kg/week [· date] |

Projected date math (`targetDate`, lines 278-283): `daysOut = ceil(|currentKg - targetKg| / rate) * 7`, added to today, formatted `en-US` long date.

---

### The exact calorie + macro math

All of it lives in `calcCaloriesDetailed` (`CalorieCalculatorModal.tsx` lines 296-320). It returns a `CalcBreakdown` that drives both the final number and the "HOW WE CALCULATED THIS" card.

**1. BMR — Mifflin? No. This is the revised Harris-Benedict equation.**

```
male:   BMR = 88.362 + 13.397·weightKg + 4.799·heightCm − 5.677·age
female: BMR = 447.593 +  9.247·weightKg + 3.098·heightCm − 4.330·age
```

- `prefer_not_to_say` uses the **male** equation.
- Height: cm used directly, or `(feet·12 + inches)·2.54` when in ft.
- Weight: lbs converted via `·0.453592` (`toKg`).
- Age: `parseInt(age) || 25` (defaults to 25 if unparseable).
- Height fallback inside the calc is 170 cm if missing.

**2. TDEE** = `BMR × multiplier` (multiplier table above).

**3. Goal adjustment** (the deficit/surplus):

```
rate = goal === 'maintain' ? 0 : (selectedRate || 0)
lose: adjustment = −(rate · 1100)   label "−{N} deficit"
gain: adjustment = +(rate · 1100)   label "+{N} surplus"
maintain: adjustment = 0
```

So the engine values **1 kg/week ≈ 1100 kcal/day**. At 0.25 kg/wk that is a 275 kcal swing; at 0.5 it is 550; at 1.0 it is 1100. (Note: this 1100 figure is a product choice, not the textbook ~1100 kcal/day-per-kg/week. It is the live constant.)

**4. Floor.** Final calories are clamped to a minimum: `1200` for female, `1500` for everyone else (`const floor = g === 'female' ? 1200 : 1500`).

```
final = max(round(TDEE + adjustment), floor)
```

**5. Result screen.** `final` count-up animates from 0 over `32` frames at `25` ms each. The breakdown card shows BMR (rounded), the activity multiplier, TDEE (rounded), and the deficit/surplus row (only when non-zero; colored red for deficit, `#10B981` green for surplus). Summary chips show Goal, Activity, Pace (if not maintain), and Age. Headline reads `Here's your plan, {firstName}` when a name is present, else the goal label.

#### Macro split

Default split is set in state: **Protein 30%, Carbs 45%, Fat 25%** (`proteinPct=30`, `carbsPct=45`, `fatPct=25`). Grams are computed by `macroGrams(cal, pct, perGram)`:

```
grams = round((calories · pct / 100) / perGram)
```

with `perGram` = **4** for protein, **4** for carbs, **9** for fat (standard Atwater factors).

Editing: a "Customize macros" toggle reveals ±/− steppers. Each tap changes a macro by **±5%**, clamped to `[5, 80]` (`Math.max(5, Math.min(80, v ± delta))`). The total badge shows when `total ≠ 100`. Save ("Start Tracking") is **disabled unless total is within 99-101%** (`totalPct < 99 || totalPct > 101`). The same 99-101 tolerance and clamp logic is duplicated in `SetGoalsScreen` (see below).

---

### SetGoalsScreen (the goal review / re-entry screen)

This is the screen `HomeScreen` opens (as a `pageSheet` modal) when the user taps "Set your daily goal", recalculates, or edits goals later. It owns the goal state and decides whether to launch the calculator.

- `isFirstTime = !initialGoals?.goal`. When first-time, the calculator is shown immediately (`showCalculator = isFirstTime`). When returning, it shows the review UI with a "Recalculate" button that re-opens the calculator pre-filled.
- State defaults if no `initialGoals`: calories `1500`, protein `30`, carbs `45`, fat `25`. (These seeded defaults are the reason the home screen must show a set-goals prompt instead of stat cards for users who never set goals — see below.)
- It renders the calorie value, a "MACRO SPLIT" stacked bar, per-macro rows (`{pct}% · {grams}g`), and a "Customize macros" editor identical in behavior to the calculator (±5%, clamp 5-80).

**Save validation + normalization** (`handleSave`, lines 174-193):

1. Reject if total `< 99` or `> 101` with an alert: `Total is {N}%. Adjust macros to be within 99-101%.`
2. If total is in range but not exactly 100, it normalizes by subtracting the `diff` from whichever macro is largest (protein, then carbs, then fat). This guarantees the saved split sums to 100.
3. Calls `onSave(goalData)` then `onBack()`.

**Macro colors** (shared across both screens): protein `#3B82F6`, carbs `#F59E0B`, fat `#8B5CF6`.

#### First-time flow → optional signup

When the first-time calculator finishes (`handleCalculatedCalories`, lines 107-155), the screen does **not** save immediately. It stages the full `GoalData` into `pendingGoalDataRef`, hides the calculator, and shows `QuickSignupScreen` (a single-tap signup so the plan persists across devices). Goals are saved **only after** signup completes or is skipped (`onComplete` → `onSave(staged)` → `onBack()`). The rationale, per the in-code comment: "we don't write a half-baked profile in case the user abandons mid-flow." `handleCalculatorBack` guards against dismissing `SetGoalsScreen` while the signup is about to render by checking `pendingGoalDataRef.current`.

For a **returning** user, the calculator just updates the calorie number and keeps existing macros; no signup.

#### The persisted model — `ExtendedGoalData`

Saved via `dataStorage.saveGoals` (AsyncStorage key `GOALS`, then Supabase sync or sync-queue if offline / not signed in). Fields (`dataStorage.ts` 143-164):

| Field | Type | Source |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `calories` | number | calculator `final` |
| `proteinPercentage` / `carbsPercentage` / `fatPercentage` | number | macro split (normalized to 100 on save) |
| `proteinGrams` / `carbsGrams` / `fatGrams` | number | `macroGrams` |
| `currentWeightKg` / `targetWeightKg` | number \| null | weight step (kg) |
| `age` | number? | derived from DOB |
| `gender` | `'male'\|'female'\|'prefer_not_to_say'`? | sex step |
| `heightCm` / `heightFeet` / `heightInches` | number? | height step |
| `goal` | `'lose'\|'maintain'\|'gain'`? | goal step |
| `activityRate` | number? | pace (`selectedRate`) |
| `activityLevel` | `'sedentary'\|'light'\|'moderate'\|'very'`? | activity step |
| `name` | string? | name step (also copied to `AccountInfo.name`) |
| `dob` | string? | `YYYY-MM-DD` |
| `trackingGoal` | string? | free-text goal, set elsewhere (not by the calculator) |

`loadGoals` is **local-first**: local AsyncStorage is the source of truth, remote (Supabase) only fills missing fields or seeds when there is no local copy at all (`{ ...remoteGoals, ...localGoals }`, lines 1257-1291). This is deliberate so a goal set offline is never reverted by a stale cloud value.

On save, `HomeScreen.handleGoalsSave` also sets `dailyCalories`, sets `goalsSet = true`, copies `goals.name` into `AccountInfo`, calls `refreshUserContext()` so every screen sees the new values immediately, and fires `analyticsService.trackOnboardingGoalSet()` (one-time) and on open `trackSetGoalsOpen()` (Mixpanel `set_goals_open`).

---

### What happens when goals are never set

This is a deliberately handled state (recent commit `145327e`, v1.2.5: "show set-goals prompt instead of fake targets for new users").

- `goalsSet` starts `false`. It flips to `true` only when `loadGoals()` returns a non-null record (on initial load, on auth hydrate, and on save).
- If goals were never set, `savedGoals` defaults would otherwise drive the stat cards to seeded values (1500 kcal and the 30/45/25 split → about 169 g / 113 g / 42 g). Showing those would assert fake targets.
- Instead, the home screen renders a **set-goals prompt card** when `!goalsSet && statsShimmerTimedOut` (`HomeScreen.tsx` line 2656). A loading shimmer runs first (an 8-second backstop) so a signed-in user whose goals are arriving from the cloud never flashes the prompt. Once that timer elapses with still no goals, the prompt appears:
  - Title: **"Set your daily goal"**
  - Subtitle: **"Add your target so we can track calories and macros."**
  - `target` icon, chevron-right, tapping it calls `handleSetGoals()` which opens the calculator (first-time path).
- Once goals exist, that card is replaced by `StatCardsSection` showing real (or bank-adjusted) calories and macros.

---

### The "re-evaluate plan" / Recalculate flow

There are two distinct re-entry paths and it is worth not confusing them:

1. **Recalculate (user-initiated, in SetGoalsScreen).** The "Recalculate" button (`refresh-cw` icon) re-opens `CalorieCalculatorScreen` with `initialData` pre-filled from current goals. Because the name already exists, `buildSteps` omits the name step (the fix for the "typed the name twice" bug). On finish for a returning user it updates only the calorie number and keeps macros.

2. **Smart weight-driven adjustment (system-initiated, separate feature).** `SmartAdjustmentModal` proposes a new calorie target when weight trends warrant it. It is not the calculator. Key rule: the proposed new calories cannot drop more than **300 below** the previous target (`minAllowed = previousCalories - 300`, "Max reduction is 300"). Editing calories re-distributes macros using the saved P/C/F energy ratios (protein·4, carbs·4, fats·9 over total). Applying it writes a new `ExtendedGoalData` via `dataStorage.saveGoals` and records an `AdjustmentRecord` in history. This belongs to the calorie-bank / adaptive-targets surface, documented in that section; it is referenced here only so an implementer does not mistake it for the onboarding calculator.

---

### Completeness notes (for the implementer)

- **Cut for scope here:** `QuickSignupScreen` internals and the Supabase goal-sync payload shape (`supabaseDataService.saveNutritionGoals`) are referenced but documented in the auth/data sections.
- **Worth knowing:** the BMR formula is **revised Harris-Benedict, not Mifflin-St Jeor.** Anyone "fixing" the math should know this is intentional, as is the `1100 kcal per kg/week` adjustment constant and the gendered floors (1200 F / 1500 other). Changing any of these silently changes every new user's target.
- **Blast radius if the floor or 1100 constant is wrong:** every onboarding target shifts; existing users are unaffected until they recalculate. The `9` for fat and `4` for protein/carbs are load-bearing in three places (calculator macros, SetGoals macros, SmartAdjustment redistribution) and must stay in sync.
- **Two duplicated implementations:** `macroGrams`, the 5-80 clamp, the 99-101 tolerance, and `MACRO_COLORS` exist in both `SetGoalsScreen.tsx` and `CalorieCalculatorModal.tsx`. Edit both or neither.

---

## 4. Home Screen and the Core Logging Loop

---

The Home screen (`src/screens/HomeScreen.tsx`, ~3229 lines) is the app hub. It owns the day's logging state, the stat cards, the input bar, and roughly two dozen modal sub-screens. It is the canonical home for the `isPremium` derivation and most account-wall touchpoints.

### Screen layout (top to bottom)

The render is a `SafeAreaView` (edges `['bottom']`) wrapping a `KeyboardAvoidingView` that holds the scroll content and the input bar so they move together with the keyboard. Order of elements:

| Order | Element | Component | Condition to render |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Top nav bar (date, greeting, menu, calendar, weight, nutrition, streak icons) | `TopNavigationBar` | always |
| 2 | Smart adjustment banner | `SmartAdjustmentBanner` | `visible={!!adjustmentAvailable}` |
| 3 | "Save your plan across devices" sign-in nudge | inline `TouchableOpacity` | `!isSignedIn` |
| 4 | "Recovery Day Used" freeze alert | inline `View` | `justFrozeToday` |
| 5 | Date selector (horizontal strip) | `DateSelector` | always, pinned |
| 6 | Stat cards OR "Set your daily goal" prompt | `StatCardsSection` / inline | scrolls with list |
| 7 | "Use it before you lose it" bank nudge | inline `View` | bank active and `bankBalance >= 200` and `remainingDays` in `[1,2]` and viewing today |
| 8 | Smart Suggest banner | `SmartSuggestBanner` | today AND `isPremium` AND `smartSuggestEnabled` |
| 9 | Pattern detection card (first of `detectedPatterns`) | `PatternDetectionCard` | today AND `detectedPatterns.length > 0` |
| 10 | Insight unlock announcement | `InsightUnlockCard` | `pendingUnlockAnnouncement && isPremium` |
| 11 | Grocery unlock card | inline `View` | `showGroceryUnlockCard` |
| 12 | First-log quote nudge | inline `View` | `showFirstLogMessage` |
| 13 | Food log list | `FoodLogSection` | always (returns `null` if no meals) |
| 14 | Cycle reset summary card | `CycleResetCard` | `showCycleResetCard && cycleResetData` |
| 15 | Exercise log list | `ExerciseLogSection` | always |
| 16 | "Ready when you are!" empty state | inline `View` | no meals, no exercises, `!hasUserTyped` |
| 17 | Floating AI Coach FAB | inline `TouchableOpacity` | `isPremium` AND not analyzing/recording |
| 18 | Bottom input bar | `BottomInputBar` | always, pinned to bottom |

The bottom spacer is a fixed `height: 160` to clear the input bar plus chips plus safe area.

### `isPremium` derivation (canonical)

Memoized in Home and threaded to every sub-screen. Premium requires both a signed-in email AND a premium grant:

```
if (!accountInfo?.email) return false;          // MUST be signed in
if (FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH) return true;            // launch flag, currently true
if (userPlan === 'premium') return true;
if (accountInfo?.premiumUntil) return new Date(accountInfo.premiumUntil) > new Date();
return false;
```

`FREE_PREMIUM_LAUNCH = true` (`src/config/featureFlags.ts:11`) grants premium to every signed-in user during launch. `isSignedIn = !!accountInfo?.email`. `accountInfo` comes from `UserContext`; Home never shadows it with local state.

---

## Stat cards (the swipeable deck)

`StatCardsSection` → `SwipeableCards` renders one card at a time from a vertically swipeable deck. Swipe threshold is `30px` (`SWIPE_THRESHOLD`), card min height `120`. Default card on mount is `macros2` (the Calories card).

Card order depends on whether the calorie bank is active:

| Bank state | Card order (swipe up cycles forward) |
|---|---|
| Inactive | `['macros2', 'macros']` |
| Active (`calorieBankActive`) | `['macros2', 'weekly', 'macros']` |

`calorieBankActive = !!(isPremium && calorieBankConfig?.enabled && calorieBankCycle)`. When the bank turns off while the Weekly card is showing, the deck falls back to `macros2`.

While goals are still hydrating (`statsLoading = !goalsSet && !statsShimmerTimedOut`), the deck renders a `StatCardSkeleton` shimmer instead. The shimmer has an 8000ms backstop (`setStatsShimmerTimedOut(true)` after 8s) so the seeded 1500 default never flashes to the real cloud number on cold open.

### Calorie card (`Macros2Card`) — Food / Exercise / Remaining

Title "Calories", pie-chart icon. Three columns separated by vertical borders. When the bank is on, a green `BANK ON` badge (`#22C55E`) sits next to the title. Values animate via `NumberTicker` (800ms).

| Column | Source value | Formula |
|---|---|---|
| Food | `currentNutrition.totalCalories` | sum of all logged food calories for the day |
| Exercise | `totalExerciseCalories` | `Σ calculateExerciseCalories(entry.exercises)` over the day's exercise entries |
| Remaining | `remainingCalories` | see below |

Remaining math (HomeScreen lines ~373-379):

```
effectiveDailyCalories = bankAdjustedCalories > 0 ? bankAdjustedCalories : 1500
remainingRaw = effectiveDailyCalories - totalCalories + totalExerciseCalories
remainingCalories = calorieBankActive ? max(0, remainingRaw) : remainingRaw
```

`bankAdjustedCalories` is `calorieBankCycle.adjustedTodayTarget` when the bank is active, else `dailyCalories`. In default (non-bank) mode Remaining is allowed to go negative so overeating is visible. In bank mode it floors at 0 (the Surplus is shown on the weekly card instead).

Remaining color (`Macros2Card.tsx:27`):

| Condition | Color |
|---|---|
| `remainingVal <= 0` | `#EF4444` (red, over budget) |
| `remainingVal < dailyCalories * 0.2` | `#F59E0B` (amber) |
| otherwise | `#10B981` (green) |

Exercise calories are added back to the budget (they increase Remaining). `calculateExerciseCalories` just sums each parsed exercise's stored `calories` (`exerciseParser.ts:164`).

### Macro grams card (`MacrosCard`)

Title "Macros", three columns Carbs / Protein / Fat, each showing `current/targetg` with a colored dot. Macro colors: protein `#3B82F6`, carbs `#F59E0B`, fat `#8B5CF6`. Targets come from `macrosData`:

```
carbs.target  = bankAdjustedMacros?.carbs   ?? savedGoals.carbsGrams   ?? 0
protein.target= bankAdjustedMacros?.protein ?? savedGoals.proteinGrams ?? 0
fat.target    = bankAdjustedMacros?.fat     ?? savedGoals.fatGrams     ?? 0
```

`bankAdjustedMacros` is `calorieBankCycle.todayMacros` when the bank is active. `current` values are `currentNutrition.total{Carbs,Protein,Fat}` from `calculateTotalNutrition(allLoggedFoods)`.

### "Set your daily goal" prompt (replaces stat cards)

When `!goalsSet && statsShimmerTimedOut`, the stat deck is replaced by a tappable card: title "Set your daily goal", subtitle "Add your target so we can track calories and macros.", target icon. Tapping it opens Set Goals. This exists so new users never see the seeded defaults (1500 kcal, 169/113/42 g) presented as real targets.

### Weekly bank card

`CalorieBankWeeklyCard` (only in the active-bank deck) shows `weeklyBudget`, `weeklyActual`, `bankBalance`, `remainingDays`, `daysInCycle` from `calorieBankCycle`. The today card deliberately does not show a live banked projection; the weekly card owns the bank balance.

---

## Date selector and calendar

### Date selector strip (`DateSelector`)

A horizontal scroll of the last **180 days** plus today (`rangeDays = 180`, loop `i` from 180 down to 0). Auto-scrolls to the end (today) on mount after a 100ms layout delay. Each day cell is `48x68`. Future dates are non-tappable (`if (date > today) return`). The active day's number sits in a `34x34` circle filled with the primary color.

Each cell shows a log-status bar (`18x3`) under the number:

| State | Bar color |
|---|---|
| `hasLog` (summary `entryCount > 0`) | `#10B981` green |
| `isMissed` (past day, no log) | `#EF4444` red |
| otherwise (today/future with no log) | transparent |

`isMissed = isPast && !hasLog`. Status is read from `summariesByDate`, not full meal data.

### Calendar modal (`CalendarModal`)

Opened from the top-bar calendar icon (`handleCalendarPress`). Receives `selectedDate`, `mealsByDate`, `dailyCalorieTarget` (`dailyCalories`), `adjustments` (`adjustmentHistory`), and `summariesByDate`. Selecting a date calls `handleDateSelect` (same handler as the strip).

### Selected-date semantics

`selectedDate` is `useState(new Date())`. `currentDateKey = format(selectedDate, 'yyyy-MM-dd')`. A `selectedDateRef` mirrors it so async logging handlers can ask "is the user still on the day they submitted on?" after an `await`. All day-scoped state is keyed by this `yyyy-MM-dd` string:

- `mealsByDate: Record<string, Meal[]>`
- `exercisesByDate: Record<string, ExerciseEntry[]>`
- `summariesByDate: Record<string, DailySummary>`

`currentDayMeals = mealsByDate[currentDateKey] || []`. Switching days triggers a `loadDay` effect that pulls only that day's shard via `dataStorage.getDailyLog(key)` and tags it on `skipPersistRef` so a pure date switch does not re-persist an unchanged shard.

---

## The three input modes

All three converge on the same bottom input bar text and ultimately on `handleInputSubmit` (text/voice) or `analyzeUploadedImage` (photo).

### Bottom input bar (`BottomInputBar`)

Left: a `Plus` button (opens photo options). Center: a multiline `TextInput`, `maxLength={500}`, `autoCapitalize="sentences"`, `autoCorrect`. Right: a single context-sensitive circle button (`36x36`):

| State | Button | Action |
|---|---|---|
| Has text | `Send` (primary bg) | `handleSubmit` → `onSubmit(trimmed)` |
| No text, not recording | `Mic` | `onMicPress` |
| Recording | `StopCircle` (error/red bg) | `onMicPress` (stops) |
| Transcribing | `Loader` spinner | disabled |

The send/mic button is disabled while `isLoading || isTranscribing`. Submitting clears the local text and any transcribed text. When the field is empty and saved prompts exist, a horizontal chip scroll (`shouldShowChips`) shows quick-prompt chips above the bar. Each chip taps to refill the input (`onQuickPromptPress`) or removes itself via an `X`. iOS shows a custom placeholder layer when unfocused and empty. The bar auto-focuses when `autoFocus` (`shouldFocusInput`) flips true (100ms delay).

Placeholder cycles by state: `"Analyzing your entry..."` / `"Recording..."` / `"Transcribing..."` / `"Describe your meal"`.

### Mode 1: Text

Type in the input, press Send → `handleInputSubmit(text)`. This is the primary path. See "Core logging loop" below.

### Mode 2: Voice (`voiceService` + `handleMicPress`)

`handleMicPress` toggles recording:

- **Start:** `voiceService.startRecording()`. Sets `isRecording`, tracks `trackVoiceRecording`. Recording config: mono, **16kHz**, **64000 bitRate**, `.m4a` (iOS `mp4`/`audioQuality 0x7F`, Android AAC encoder). On failure shows a permission/error alert.
- **Stop:** `voiceService.stopRecording()` stops, gets the file URI, then `transcribeWithOpenAI`. The file is read as base64 and sent through `invokeWhisper` (the Edge Function proxy — never OpenAI directly). The transcription is set into `transcribedText`, which syncs into the input bar; the user reviews then presses Send. On transcription failure the service returns `null` (not a sentinel sentence) and the handler shows "Failed to transcribe audio. Please try typing instead."

A `BarVisualizer` (20 bars, height 15-60) renders above the input while recording.

### Mode 3: Photo (`PhotoOptionsModal` flow)

Tapping `Plus` opens `PhotoOptionsModal` with two options:

- `handleTakePhoto` → sets `pendingActionRef = 'camera'`, closes modal.
- `handleUploadPhoto` → sets `pendingActionRef = 'library'`, closes modal.

The modal must fully dismiss before launching the picker (avoids a known modal-stacking bug). `handleModalDismiss` (300ms after dismiss) or a fallback effect (800ms) calls `openCameraAfterModalClose` / `openLibraryAfterModalClose`. Both:

1. Check/request permission (camera or media library) with a **10000ms** timeout. Permanently-denied shows a settings alert.
2. Launch picker: `mediaTypes: Images`, `allowsEditing: false`, `quality: 0.8`.
3. On a chosen asset: set `uploadedImage`, `uploadFileName`, show `ImageUploadStatus`, and call `simulateUpload(uri)`.

`simulateUpload` fakes a progress bar (`+= random()*15` per 300ms tick) to 100%, switches status to `analyzing`, then after 300ms calls `analyzeUploadedImage`. The real work is `analyzeFoodFromImage(uri)` (OpenAI Vision via proxy), raced against a **30000ms** timeout. On success a `Meal` with `prompt: "Image"`, `imageUri`, and parsed foods is committed via `commitMealChange`; entry count increments; analytics + referral progress fire. On no-food it sets status `failed` with "No food detected" (retryable via `handleRetryUpload`).

The photo path uses the same `canAddEntry()` gate as text (single source of truth for the free daily limit, currently disabled). It also increments the entry count exactly like text — earlier it did not, which broke the account-wall nag and re-showed the first-log banner for photo-only users.

---

## Optimistic UI: pending skeleton meals

Text submission renders an instant skeleton so the UI never blocks on the network.

1. `handleInputSubmit` dismisses the keyboard, trims, runs the entry gate.
2. Builds a `pendingMeal` with a generated `id`, `summary: "Crunching the meal..."`, empty `foods`, `isLoading: true`, `loadingState: 'analyzing'`.
3. Immediately appends it to `mealsByDate[currentDateKey]`.

In `FoodLogSection`, a meal with `isLoading` renders a skeleton bar plus a spinner and a randomly chosen italic message from `PARSING_MESSAGES` (15 phrases, e.g. "Crunching the numbers on those calories...", "Consulting the macro oracle..."). The header shows a `RotatingTitle` cycling 6 `LOADING_TITLES` every 2000ms ("Crunching the meal...", "Analyzing your plate...", etc.). Delete/edit/bookmark controls are hidden while loading.

Crucially, pending skeletons are never persisted. `saveDailyLog` filters out any meal with `isLoading` or `loadingState === 'analyzing'` (`dataStorage.ts:1311`) so a reload mid-analysis cannot resurrect a permanently-stuck "calculating" row.

---

## Core logging loop (`handleInputSubmit`)

Full flow for a text/voice submission (HomeScreen ~1457-1646):

1. **Guard:** trim; bail on empty. `canAddEntry()` gate (returns `true` pre-launch — the 3/day free limit is TODO-disabled at `HomeScreen.tsx:1422`). When re-enabled it shows a "Daily Limit Reached" alert offering the subscription screen.
2. **Optimistic insert** of the pending skeleton (above).
3. **Analyze:** `analyzeFoodWithChatGPT(trimmed)` via the proxy.
   - **Clarification:** if the result has `clarificationQuestion`, remove the pending meal, restore the text into the input (`setTranscribedText`, `setShouldFocusInput`), and alert "Clarification Needed".
   - **Key not configured:** `OPENAI_API_KEY_NOT_CONFIGURED` → remove pending, alert "Food Analysis Not Configured".
4. **First-log nudge:** if `entryCount === 0`, set `showFirstLogMessage`.
5. **Foods found:** build `finalizedMeal` (`isLoading: false`, `loadingState: 'done'`) and **upsert** it via `commitMealChange`. The upsert is a deliberate map-or-append: if a wholesale reload wiped the pending row mid-flight (`!hasPending`), it appends instead of silently dropping the parsed food. Then `incrementEntryCount`, `trackMealLogged(selectedDate)`, and (if signed in) `referralService.processMealLoggingProgress`. Returns `true`.
6. **No foods → try exercise:** `parseExerciseInput(trimmed)`. If it parses, remove the pending meal, push a new `ExerciseEntry` to `exercisesByDate`, `incrementEntryCount`, `trackExerciseLogged`. (Same input box handles both food and exercise.)
7. **Nothing detected:** remove pending, alert "No Entry Detected … Try adding more detail or separate your entries."
8. **Error:** remove pending, alert "Error … Please try again."

`handleInputSubmit` returns `true` only when a meal is actually logged. `SmartSuggestBanner.handleLog` relies on this exact return to avoid claiming "Meal Logged" when the log aborted (clarification, no food, error).

### Two helpers that protect against day-switch data loss

- `commitMealChange(dateKey, updater)`: if the user is still on `dateKey`, update state (persist effect saves it). If they navigated away, the day is no longer in memory, so it reads the persisted shard, applies the updater, and `saveDailyLog`s it directly — then refreshes summaries. This is the fix for a meal that finished analyzing after a day switch overwriting the wrong day.
- `removePendingMeal(dateKey, pendingId)`: only touches state and only if still on that day (skeletons are never persisted, so there is nothing to clean up if the user left).

### Persistence effect

A `useEffect` on `mealsByDate` (skipping the `skipPersistRef`-tagged hydration object) runs `persistAndSync`: `saveMeals` → reload summaries → smart-reminder effectiveness check → grocery-unlock check (premium) → reload summaries again → `checkInsightUnlocks`. Exercises persist via a separate effect on `exercisesByDate`.

---

## Meal and exercise CRUD

| Action | Handler | Behavior |
|---|---|---|
| Tap a food row | `FoodLogSection.handleFoodPress` | Opens the food-detail slide-up modal (95% screen height, drag-to-dismiss at `dy > 100` or `vy > 0.5`) |
| Edit macros of a food | modal Save → `onUpdateFood` | Recomputes calories as `round(P*4 + C*4 + F*9)`, floored at 0; saves the shard via `saveDailyLog`; calls `updateFoodCache(prompt, foods, summary)` so future logs of the same prompt use the corrected values |
| Remove one food | `handleRemoveFood(foodId)` | Filters the food out of its meal; **removes the meal entirely if it has no foods left**; tracks `trackFoodItemRemoval` |
| Edit a meal prompt | `handleEditMealPrompt(mealId, newPrompt)` | Re-runs `analyzeFoodWithChatGPT`; handles clarification/no-food/error; on success replaces `prompt` + `foods` via `commitMealChange`, increments entry count, tracks `trackMealPromptEdit`. Shows the blocking `isAnalyzingFood` overlay |
| Delete a whole meal | `handleDeleteMeal(mealId)` | Confirm alert "Delete Prompt" → filters the meal out of the day |
| Delete an exercise entry | `handleDeleteExerciseEntry(entryId)` | Confirm alert "Delete Exercise Log" → filters it out |
| Bookmark / save a prompt | `handleToggleSavePrompt(meal)` | Toggles saving `meal.summary || meal.prompt` (AI-refined summary preferred) into `savedPrompts`, capped at `MAX_SAVED_PROMPTS = 6`, dedup by normalized lowercase text |
| Reuse a saved prompt | `handleSelectSavedPrompt` | Fills the input and focuses it |

The food-detail modal also exposes an editable **Nutrition Facts** table covering ~26 fields (total carbs, fiber, sugar, added sugars, sugar alcohols, net carbs, protein, total/saturated/trans/poly/mono fat, omega-3, cholesterol, sodium, calcium, iron, magnesium, zinc, potassium, vitamins A/C/D/E/K/B12). Editing P/C/F there also recomputes calories with the 4/4/9 rule. Editing calories directly scales every macro and micro by the ratio `newCalories / oldCalories`.

The blocking `isAnalyzingFood` overlay (a centered blurred card with spinner, title "Analyzing", subtitle "Identifying food and macros...") is used for edits and photo analysis, fading in/out over 220ms. The primary text path deliberately does not use it (it uses the inline skeleton instead).

---

## Day-sharding storage model

Meals are stored one AsyncStorage key per day, not one blob.

- **Key shape:** `@trackkal:log:<yyyy-MM-dd>` (`STORAGE_KEYS.dailyLog(date)`, `dataStorage.ts:118`).
- **Read one day:** `getDailyLog(date)` → `MealEntry[]`.
- **Write one day:** `saveDailyLog(date, meals)` under a per-date write lock (`withWriteLock('log:'+date)`). It: filters out optimistic skeletons; diffs against the previously persisted list to compute `removedIds` (so removed meals are soft-deleted in Supabase, not just locally); writes the shard; invalidates the in-memory meals cache; calls `updateSummaryForDate`; then fires `syncMealsToSupabase` (fire-and-forget, never blocks UX).
- **`saveMeals(mealsByDate)`:** legacy-compatible wrapper that loops and `saveDailyLog`s each date.
- **`loadMeals()`:** reconstructs the full blob (used by auth/foreground reloads); the doc-comment warns to prefer `getDailyLog`.
- **Migrations on load:** `migrateLegacyMealsToShards()` converts the old single `@trackkal:meals` blob into per-day shards (then deletes it); `migrateMealsToSummaries()` ensures every day has a `DailySummary`.

### Summaries (the cheap day index)

`DailySummary` (`dataStorage.ts:307`) is stored as a single map at `@trackkal:summaries` and holds `date`, `totalCalories/Protein/Carbs/Fat`, `entryCount`, `updatedAt`, plus optional micros. Summaries power the streak calc, the date-strip status dots, the calendar, calorie-bank cycles, and insight-unlock stats — all without loading per-day meal shards. `entryCount > 0` is the canonical "this day has a log" test used everywhere.

---

## First-log nudge

On the very first ever entry (`entryCount === 0`), `setShowFirstLogMessage(true)` shows a one-time quote card above the food list:

> "Most people improve simply by paying attention."

It auto-hides after **6000ms** (effect on `showFirstLogMessage`) so it does not stay pinned for the session. It fires from both the text path and the photo path.

---

## Streak and account-wall touchpoints on Home

### Streak

`currentStreak = calculateStreak(summariesByDate, streakFreeze?.usedOnDates || [])`. Shown in the top bar (with a frozen indicator) and in the `StreakWidgetCard` modal (tapped via `handleStreakPress`).

- **Streak reminder notification:** if today is not yet logged and `currentStreak > 0`, schedules a local notification at **22:00** (id `streak-reminder-<today>`): title `🔥 Don't lose your streak!`, body referencing the day count. Cancelled the moment today is logged.
- **Streak freeze (premium):** `freezesAvailable` resets to **2** at the start of each month (`lastResetDate` = `yyyy-MM-01`). `checkMissedDaysAndFreeze` auto-consumes a freeze when yesterday was missed but a streak was alive the day before; on use it sets `justFrozeToday` which swaps the greeting for the "Recovery Day Used" card. Runs on load and on every app foreground.

### Account wall (mandatory sign-up nag)

`AccountWallModal` is the accountless-user funnel. Two triggers, both gated on `!accountInfo?.email`:

| Trigger | Condition | Delay |
|---|---|---|
| On open | `goalsSet && entryCount >= 5` (effect on `goalsSet`) | 1500ms |
| On log | inside `incrementEntryCount`, when `next >= 5 && next % 5 === 0` | 800ms |

So the wall appears once goals are set and 5+ logs exist, and re-nags every 5th log (5, 10, 15…) rather than on every meal. Continuing from the wall opens `AccountScreen` in `signup` mode with `accountFromWall = true` so Back returns to Home (not Settings). A lighter always-on touchpoint is the persistent "Save your plan across devices" bar shown whenever `!isSignedIn`.

---

## What I cut, the next 80%, worries, blast radius

**Cut for scope (in adjacent sections):** the full calorie-bank cycle engine math (`adjustedTodayTarget`, `todayMacros`, banking/spending caps) — only its Home-facing reads are covered here; the insight-unlock thresholds; `analyzeFoodWithChatGPT`/`analyzeFoodFromImage` prompt internals and the `ParsedFood` schema; `chatCoachService.buildContext` data-quality gating used by Smart Suggest.

**Next 80%:** document the `dataStorage` sync layer (write locks, Supabase merge, cache TTL) and the summary-recalc path end to end; the Set Goals macro math that produces `proteinGrams/carbsGrams/fatGrams`; the Smart Suggest prompt and its `forceHungry`/`forceNew` cache behavior.

**Worth worrying about:** the free 3/day limit is currently disabled (`canAddEntry()` returns `true`, `HomeScreen.tsx:1422`) yet the "Daily Limit Reached" alerts and copy still ship — re-enabling it is a one-line change with user-visible blast radius. The photo upload progress bar is fully simulated (`simulateUpload` random ticks), not real network progress; a slow Vision call still shows 100% then sits in "analyzing".

**Blast radius if Home logic breaks:** `handleInputSubmit`, `commitMealChange`, and the `saveDailyLog` skeleton filter are the load-bearing trio. A regression in any of them risks the historical bugs called out in the code: dropped parsed foods, wrong-day writes wiping a day, or stuck "calculating" rows persisting forever.

---

## 5. The AI System: Every Prompt, the Proxy, Schemas, Sanitization and Caching

---

TrackKcal makes **10 distinct OpenAI calls**: 9 LLM prompts plus Whisper voice transcription. Two more food-logging paths (`exerciseParser.ts`, `GrocerySuggestionService.ts`) are fully deterministic and never touch an LLM. Every LLM call routes through one function (`invokeAI`) which hits one Supabase Edge Function (`ai-proxy`). The OpenAI key lives only on Supabase. The client never sees it.

### Quick reference: every LLM call

| # | Name | Function / File | Model | Temp | max_tokens | Output format | `call_type` tag | Cached? | Premium? |
|---|------|-----------------|-------|------|-----------|---------------|-----------------|---------|----------|
| 1 | Agentic Food Analysis (3-stage) | `analyzeFoodWithChatGPT` / `openaiService.ts` | `gpt-4o` | 0.3 | none | `json_schema` strict (`food_analysis`) | `food-analysis` | Yes — AsyncStorage, prompt-hash tagged | Core (free) |
| 2 | Nutrition Factors (per-100g library) | `fetchNutritionFactors` / `openaiService.ts` | `gpt-4o-mini` | 0.2 | none | `json_schema` strict (`nutrition_factors`) | `nutrition-factors` | Saved to food reference store | Core (free) |
| 3 | Food Image Vision (describer) | `analyzeFoodFromImage` / `openaiService.ts` | `gpt-4o` | 0.3 | 300 | free text | `food-image-vision` | No | Camera-log feature |
| 4 | Weekly Insights | `generateWeeklyInsights` / `openaiService.ts` | `gpt-4o-mini` | 0.4 | 600 | free text | `weekly-insights` | Cached per week by caller | Premium insight (unlock-gated) |
| 5 | AI Nutrition Coach | `getCoachChatResponse` / `openaiService.ts` + `chatCoachService.ts` | `gpt-4o` | 0.7 | 600 | free text | `coach-chat` | No (no memory) | Rate-limited free + premium |
| 6 | Smart Suggest | `generateSmartSuggestion` / `openaiService.ts` | `gpt-4o-mini` | 0.3 | none | `json_schema` strict (`smart_suggestion`) | `smart-suggestion` | Yes — once/day, date-keyed | Home banner |
| 7 | Pattern Detection | `analyzePatterns` / `patternDetectionService.ts` | `gpt-4o-mini` | 0.3 | none | `json_schema` strict (`pattern_detection`) | `pattern-detection` | Detected patterns stored 14 days | Premium |
| 8 | Grocery Coach (explainer) | `getGroceryCoachExplanation` / `groceryCoachService.ts` | `gpt-4o-mini` | 0.5 | 450 | `json_schema` strict (`grocery_coach`) | `grocery-coach` | No | Grocery feature |
| 9 | Deficit & Surplus Impact | inline in `generateDeficitInsight` / `WeightTrackerScreen.tsx` | `gpt-4o-mini` | 0.7 | 100 | free text | **none (untagged)** | Cached per week (`@trackkal:deficitInsight`) | Weight Tracker insight |
| — | Confidence Improvement Hint | `generateConfidenceHint` / `openaiService.ts` | `gpt-4o-mini` | 0.4 | 150 | `json_schema` strict (`confidence_hint`) | `confidence-hint` | Yes — prompt-hash tagged | Tap a low/medium badge |
| — | Whisper Voice Transcription | `invokeWhisper` / `voiceService.ts` | `whisper-1` | — | — | plain text (`{ text }`) | hard-coded `whisper-transcription` in Sentry tags | No | Voice-log feature |

Note: the repo brief and the audit say "around 9 prompts." The live code has **10 LLM prompts** because Confidence Hint (added with the json_schema migration) is not in the `2026-04-30` audit. Treat the audit as historical: it predates the migration to strict `json_schema`, the confidence field, prompt versioning, and the identity/weight guardrails. The code below is authoritative.

Which prompts return strict JSON vs free text:
- **Strict `json_schema` (6):** Food Analysis, Nutrition Factors, Smart Suggest, Pattern Detection, Grocery Coach, Confidence Hint.
- **Free text (4):** Image Vision (describer), Weekly Insights, Coach Chat, Deficit & Surplus. This matches the architecture non-negotiable: "All 5 JSON returning prompts use strict json_schema" was the old count; it is now 6.

---

### Prompt 1 — Agentic Food Analysis (the core engine)
